<div class="marriage-display-ws"><div style="display:inline-block;line-height:normal;margin-top:1px;white-space:normal;">Deen Kharbouch</div>
   <div class="marriage-line-margin2px">&#8203;</div>&#32;<div style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:1px;">&#8203;</div>&#40;<abbr title="married">m.</abbr>&#160;2007&#59;&#32;<abbr title="divorced">div.</abbr>&#160;2014&#41;<wbr />&#8203;</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">1</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://frenchmontana.com">frenchmontana<wbr />.com</a></span>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div>
<p><b>Karim Kharbouch</b> (<a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Arabic" title="Moroccan Arabic">Arabic</a>: <span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar" dir="rtl">ŸÉÿ±ŸäŸÖ ÿÆÿ±ÿ®Ÿàÿ¥</span></span> <a href="/wiki/IPA_pronunciation" class="mw-redirect" title="IPA pronunciation">[k√¶…æiÀêm œá…ë…æbuÀê É]</a>; born November 9, 1984), better known by his stage name <b>French Montana</b>, is a Moroccan-American rapper.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, he immigrated to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> with his family at the age of 13.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SDinterview_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDinterview-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He embarked on a musical career in 2002, releasing a slew of independent material until signing a joint-venture record deal with <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Puff Daddy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">Maybach Music Group</a> in 2012.
</p><p>Kharbouch released his debut mixtape in 2007 and had his first breakthrough with the single "Choppa Choppa Down" in 2010. He released his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Excuse_My_French_(album)" title="Excuse My French (album)">Excuse My French</a></i> in May 2013, which was met with generally mixed reviews despite commercial success from its lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Pop_That_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pop That (song)">Pop That</a>" (featuring Rick Ross, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In July 2017, he released his second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Jungle_Rules" title="Jungle Rules">Jungle Rules</a></i>, which peaked at number three on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>. The album was preceded by the hit single "<a href="/wiki/Unforgettable_(French_Montana_song)" title="Unforgettable (French Montana song)">Unforgettable</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Swae_Lee" title="Swae Lee">Swae Lee</a>), which became Montana's first song as lead artist to reach the top 10 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">U.S. <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, also becoming <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification#List_of_certifications" title="RIAA certification">diamond certified</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>. His third and fourth studio albums, <i><a href="/wiki/Montana_(French_Montana_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Montana (French Montana album)">Montana</a></i> (2019) and <i><a href="/wiki/They_Got_Amnesia" title="They Got Amnesia">They Got Amnesia</a></i> (2021) were released to lukewarm commercial and critical response.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>French Montana has founded the record label Coke Boys Records (previously known as Cocaine City Records) in 2008, and has signed Chicago rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Durk" title="Lil Durk">Lil Durk</a>, fellow New York artists including <a href="/wiki/Velous" title="Velous">Velous</a>, the late <a href="/wiki/Chinx" title="Chinx">Chinx</a>, and record producer <a href="/wiki/Harry_Fraud" title="Harry Fraud">Harry Fraud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He is the most <a href="/wiki/Music_streaming_service" title="Music streaming service">streamed</a> African-born musical artist, and is the first African-born artist to have a <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">RIAA certified</a> <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_certification" title="Music recording certification">diamond</a> song. Outside of music, French Montana has been prolific in charitable and <a href="#Philanthropy">philanthropic endeavors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Karim Kharbouch was born on November 9, 1984, in <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He grew up at the family estate outside <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a> where he lived for the first 13 years of his life.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Growing up, he was consumed with <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> and rap, describing them as his two favorite childhood hobbies,<sup id="cite_ref-SDinterview_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDinterview-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> before getting into basketball in his later teens.<sup id="cite_ref-CombatJack1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CombatJack1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the mid-1990s, Kharbouch left Morocco with his parents and younger brother for <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, where they settled in the <a href="/wiki/South_Bronx" title="South Bronx">South Bronx</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Kharbouch spoke only his <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Morocco" title="Languages of Morocco">native languages</a> of <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Darija" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan Darija">Moroccan Darija</a> Arabic and <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Morocco" title="French language in Morocco">French</a> when he first arrived, and learned <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> in the streets and in the Bronx high schools of <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt_High_School_(New_York_City)" title="Theodore Roosevelt High School (New York City)">Roosevelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herbert_H._Lehman_High_School" title="Herbert H. Lehman High School">Lehman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> After struggling for two years, his father decided they would move back to Casablanca, but his mother opted to stay back with their children citing lack of opportunities back home.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> His mother was pregnant with his youngest brother at the time, who was born in the United States shortly after his father departed for Morocco. With three children, his mother was dependent on welfare for financial support. Kharbouch eventually found himself the primary breadwinner for the family.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2002.E2.80.932010:_Cocaine_City_Records"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002‚Äì2010:_Cocaine_City_Records">2002‚Äì2010: Cocaine City Records</span></h3>
<p>French Montana began his career as a <a href="/wiki/Battle_rap" title="Battle rap">battle rapper</a> in his teens under the name Young French. In 2002, French and close friend Cams created a series of street DVDs called <i>Cocaine City</i>, drawing inspiration from the <i>Smack</i> DVD series popular at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IndieHipHop_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndieHipHop-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The series featured interviews with major and upcoming rappers, personalities, and a focus on street music and hip hop beefs.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RapFixLive_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RapFixLive-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Initially as Young French, he used the DVDs as a means of showcasing his talent as an underground artist, including in it his own original music, freestyles, and collaborations with other artists. The first volume in the series featured <a href="/wiki/Pee_Wee_Kirkland" title="Pee Wee Kirkland">Pee Wee Kirkland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CombatJack1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CombatJack1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> What started out as a medium for developing an audience, quickly grew into one of the top-selling street DVDs.<sup id="cite_ref-IndieHipHop_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndieHipHop-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The series ran for eight years between 2002 and 2010, totaling 14 volumes, and multiple spinoff films. Based out of the Bronx, French ran the series with the help of childhood friends including Brock, Droop Pop and Cheeze, who went on to become the first rappers that formed the Coke Boys.<sup id="cite_ref-HHVibeBrock_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HHVibeBrock-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HypeBrock_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HypeBrock-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, French suffered a gunshot to the head when he was confronted by two armed gunmen as he was leaving a recording studio in the Bronx.<sup id="cite_ref-Life+Times_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life+Times-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USmag_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USmag-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The incident resulted in one of the gunmen dead, in what is believed to be a case of "<a href="/wiki/Friendly_fire" title="Friendly fire">friendly fire</a>" by one assailant against the other.<sup id="cite_ref-Life+Times_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life+Times-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CombatJack3_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CombatJack3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> French was then hospitalized for several weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CombatJack3_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CombatJack3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Upon discharge, he discovered that he was set up by someone close to him and his circle.<sup id="cite_ref-Life+Times_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life+Times-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, French Montana released his debut mixtape <i>French Revolution Vol. 1</i>, which included collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Murda" title="Uncle Murda">Uncle Murda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jae_Millz" title="Jae Millz">Jae Millz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazaradi_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazaradi Fox">Mazaradi Fox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Yayo" title="Tony Yayo">Tony Yayo</a>. The track "Quarter to Eight" was the first of many collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>. The <a href="/wiki/J.Cardim" class="mw-redirect" title="J.Cardim">J.Cardim</a>-produced "Straight Cash" was French's first underground hit. In 2008, he released his second mixtape, <i>Live From Africa</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The song "Waavvy" was the first collaboration with rapper <a href="/wiki/Max_B" title="Max B">Max B</a>.
</p><p>French Montana and Max B released their debut collaborative mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Coke_Wave" title="Coke Wave">Coke Wave</a></i> on February 6, 2009. A few weeks later, on February 23, Max B's mixtape <i>Quarantine</i> was released, while French released his <i>The Laundry Man</i> on February 24, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The two artists resumed concentrating on their solo records, until the release of their second collaborative mixtape <i>Coke Wave 2</i> in November that year.
</p><p>French was included in <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a>'s Freshman Class of 2012. At that time he had already been signed to <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a> following the success of his single "Shot Caller", and had just signed a joint-venture between Bad Boy and <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">Maybach Music Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RapFixLive_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RapFixLive-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Fraud_and_the_Chinatown_raid">Harry Fraud and the Chinatown raid</span></h4>
<p>In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine, close friend and producer <a href="/wiki/Harry_Fraud" title="Harry Fraud">Harry Fraud</a> revealed first meeting French Montana during a recording session at a studio in <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Chinatown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HarryFraudRS_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarryFraudRS-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Fraud recalls recording a song for someone which French happened to have a guest feature on. In an unusual turn of events, the building was <a href="/wiki/Police_raid" title="Police raid">raided</a> by police after a tip-off that there were counterfeit Gucci and Louis Vuitton purses being manufactured at the same building.<sup id="cite_ref-HarryFraudRS_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarryFraudRS-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Having lost his studio spot, Fraud went on to form his own studio in Brooklyn, where the two "met and formed a bond".<sup id="cite_ref-HarryFraudRS_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarryFraudRS-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Harry Fraud, who hails from a musical family background and had interned at a <a href="/wiki/Recording_studio" title="Recording studio">recording studio</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HarryFraudL+T_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarryFraudL+T-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> was still unknown professionally at the time. The two released their first collaboration "New York Minute", featuring <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>, off of French's fifth mixtape <i>Mac Wit Da Cheese</i> released on April 19, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-FM5_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM5-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Following its success, the two artists recorded "We Playin In The Wind" off of French's sixth mixtape <i>The Laundry Man 2</i> released on June 29.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> With "New York Minute" still buzzing in the city, rapper <a href="/wiki/Ma$e" class="mw-redirect" title="Ma$e">Ma$e</a> would approach French Montana to hop on the remix,<sup id="cite_ref-ChoppaRoss_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChoppaRoss-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> included in French's eighth mixtape <i>Coke Wave 2</i> released in November. Since then, Harry Fraud's production has been a staple among French's music, and Fraud has since ventured out into working with various other artists. Fraud gained mainstream attention when his track with French Montana "<a href="/wiki/Shot_Caller_(French_Montana_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shot Caller (French Montana song)">Shot Caller</a>" became one of the most added tracks on <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban contemporary">urban contemporary</a> radio in 2011‚Äì2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SDinterview_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDinterview-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaby_Acevedo_and_signing_with_Akon">Gaby Acevedo and signing with Akon</span></h4>
<p>Starting in 2009, French Montana had signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Konvict_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Konvict Music">Konvict Music</a> label.<sup id="cite_ref-AkonAcevedo_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AkonAcevedo-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The two previously met in Miami in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and later appeared on <a href="/wiki/DJ_Green_Lantern" title="DJ Green Lantern">DJ Green Lantern</a>'s "Invasion Radio" on <a href="/wiki/SiriusXM" class="mw-redirect" title="SiriusXM">SiriusXM</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hip-Hop_Nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip-Hop Nation">Hip-Hop Nation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The pair collaborated on a series of tracks including their first single "Married to the Streets" on French's seventh mixtape <i>Cocaine Konvicts</i> released on September 25.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GabyAcevedo_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GabyAcevedo-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In later interviews, French revealed that he had a "shopping deal" with Akon for a six months to a year period.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ParleMag_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParleMag-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> "A shopping deal is when an artist takes a liking in you, and they try to take you to a label to get you signed. I was gonna go get signed to his label, but they were going through problems with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope</a>. [As a result] my deal was over with him, so I went and did my own thing", claimed French in his 2012 interview with Complex.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Akon, whom French refers to as "big brother",<sup id="cite_ref-BadBoyKonvict_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BadBoyKonvict-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> would continue to maintain a relationship with French, collaborating on songs together despite the unsuccessful deal between the two.
</p><p>French had met Akon through their mutual friend Gaby Acevedo.<sup id="cite_ref-AkonAcevedo_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AkonAcevedo-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GabyAcevedo_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GabyAcevedo-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Acevedo was then-president of <a href="/wiki/SRC_Records" title="SRC Records">SRC Records</a> ‚Äì under founder and chairman <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rifkind" title="Steve Rifkind">Steve Rifkind</a> ‚Äî the label first responsible for breaking out artists such as Akon, <a href="/wiki/David_Banner" title="David Banner">David Banner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a>, then a member of Fat Joe's <a href="/wiki/Terror_Squad_(group)" title="Terror Squad (group)">Terror Squad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GabyAcevedo_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GabyAcevedo-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Acevedo, whom French had befriended during his time working on the <i>Cocaine City</i> DVDs, had put his music on to Akon who then approached French inviting him to meet him in <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AkonAcevedo_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AkonAcevedo-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GabyAcevedo_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GabyAcevedo-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Although the Akon deal was short-lived, Acevedo would eventually go on to become French's manager following his mainstream breakout. In 2012, with Rifkind leaving SRC's parent company <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a> in September, the SRC imprint would close shop as well. With French's management deal with Mizay Entertainment having recently ended, Gaby Acevedo would postpone retirement to become his new manager, where he now spends his time on the road touring with French.<sup id="cite_ref-GabyAcevedo_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GabyAcevedo-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932011:_.22Choppa_Choppa_Down.22_and_southern_breakout"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010‚Äì2011:_&quot;Choppa_Choppa_Down&quot;_and_southern_breakout">2010‚Äì2011: "Choppa Choppa Down" and southern breakout</span></h3>
<p>French released his tenth mixtape <i>Coke Boys</i> on September 15, 2010, which included collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Three_6_Mafia" title="Three 6 Mafia">Three 6 Mafia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gucci_Mane" title="Gucci Mane">Gucci Mane</a>, Akon, <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a>, fellow Coke Boys, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-FM10_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM10-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The record which included the track "Choppa Choppa Down", featuring <a href="/wiki/Waka_Flocka_Flame" title="Waka Flocka Flame">Waka Flocka Flame</a>, became a hit among clubs and radio throughout the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">south</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guide_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guide-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Waka Flocka, who recently broken into the mainstream with his single "<a href="/wiki/Hard_In_Da_Paint" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard In Da Paint">Hard In Da Paint</a>" released on May 13, had recorded the song earlier that year while Gucci Mane was still in prison. An early remix to the song, featuring French Montana, was included in French's ninth mixtape <i>Mac &amp; Cheese 2</i> released earlier that year on May 6 and which also included collaborations with rising stars <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, Nicki Minaj, <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curren$y" class="mw-redirect" title="Curren$y">Curren$y</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nipsey_Hussle" title="Nipsey Hussle">Nipsey Hussle</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-FM9_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM9-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The two respective breakout tracks would kick off the start of a close relationship between French and Waka Flocka, where the two describe themselves as being "brothers".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Signing_with_Debra_Antney">Signing with Debra Antney</span></h4>
<p>On November 18, 2010, <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a> magazine reported on French Montana having signed with <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>-based management firm Mizay Entertainment, headed by Debra Antney.<sup id="cite_ref-XXLmizay_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXLmizay-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Debra, who is Waka Flocka's mother, was also manager to Gucci Mane, <a href="/wiki/OJ_Da_Juiceman" class="mw-redirect" title="OJ Da Juiceman">OJ Da Juiceman</a>, rising star <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luger_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lex Luger (musician)">Lex Luger</a> and the <a href="/wiki/808_Mafia" title="808 Mafia">808 Mafia</a> production team, and formerly <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> prior to her mainstream breakout.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The music video for "Choppa Choppa Down",<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> which featured a <a href="/wiki/Black_Hawk_Down_(film)" title="Black Hawk Down (film)">Black Hawk Down</a> theme, was released in late-January and included cameos from Gucci, <a href="/wiki/Shawty_Lo" title="Shawty Lo">Shawty Lo</a>, DJ Holiday and members of <a href="/wiki/Brick_Squad_Monopoly" class="mw-redirect" title="Brick Squad Monopoly">Brick Squad Monopoly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> With the success of the <i>Coke Boys</i> mixtape and his recent management deal with Debra, French adopted a recurring <a href="/wiki/Trap_music_(hip_hop)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trap music (hip hop)">trap</a> influence among his music. in 2013, Debra Antney sued French Montana for dealing behind her back for commission. In 2017, Debra won the <a href="/wiki/Lawsuit" title="Lawsuit">lawsuit</a> against him for which he was obliged to pay $2 million to Debra.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 15, French released his eleventh mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Mister_16:_Casino_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="Mister 16: Casino Life">Mister 16: Casino Life</a></i>, which featured productions from Fraud and <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luger" title="Lex Luger">Lex Luger</a> among others, including his soon-to-be next hit "Shot Caller".<sup id="cite_ref-FM11_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM11-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The tape's combination of hard trap beats alongside the more soulful beats ‚Äì such as those of his New York producer Harry Fraud ‚Äì would become a fixture among French's music. The latter sound being further explored in his twelfth mixtape <i>Coke Boys 2</i> released on August 19,<sup id="cite_ref-FM12_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM12-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> providing a softer break from his more robust tapes that year. Both records have been acclaimed for their production and hooks. French would continue on his increasing presence in the South, releasing his collaborative mixtape with Waka Flocka called <i>Lock Out</i> on December 14. That same month, he would release his long-awaited collaborative mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Cocaine_Mafia" title="Cocaine Mafia">Cocaine Mafia</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis</a>-based rappers <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a> and <a href="/wiki/Project_Pat" title="Project Pat">Project Pat</a>, released on December 19.<sup id="cite_ref-FM14_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM14-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> This would be French's thirteenth and fourteenth mixtapes, respectively. With four records out in 2011, it would be his busiest year of releases since 2009. In a 2012 interview with Parl√© magazine, French revealed his deal with Mizay Entertainment as having been for a year and a half.<sup id="cite_ref-ParleMag_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParleMag-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaborating_with_Rick_Ross">Collaborating with Rick Ross</span></h4>
<p>With French's growing buzz in the South, he was approached by <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> who invited him to his studio.<sup id="cite_ref-ChoppaRoss_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChoppaRoss-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> French, who admits having been a fan of Ross' music, was invited to come "at like three in the morning" where he listened to his upcoming <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">MMG</a> collaborative album <i><a href="/wiki/Self_Made_Vol._1" title="Self Made Vol. 1">Self Made Vol. 1</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ChoppaRoss_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChoppaRoss-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The two recorded a track for the album, while Ross hopped on the remix to "Choppa Choppa Down".<sup id="cite_ref-ChoppaRoss_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChoppaRoss-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The new single, which also featured Wiz Khalifa, was released on April 28, 2011, with the music video coming out in June.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> An earlier remix featuring Gucci Mane and Wiz Khalifa had been released on March 25. The collaboration would mark the start of French's relationship with Rick Ross and his <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">Maybach Music Group</a>, prompting speculation whether French would be signing to the label.<sup id="cite_ref-ChoppaRoss_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChoppaRoss-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932012:_.22Shot_Caller.22_and_New_York_takeover"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011‚Äì2012:_&quot;Shot_Caller&quot;_and_New_York_takeover">2011‚Äì2012: "Shot Caller" and New York takeover</span></h3>
<p>With French juggling between Atlanta and New York, his song "<a href="/wiki/Shot_Caller_(French_Montana_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shot Caller (French Montana song)">Shot Caller</a>" off of the <i>Casino Life</i> record would gain traction on New York radio beginning mid-2011. During an on-air interview with <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a> on <a href="/wiki/DJ_Green_Lantern" title="DJ Green Lantern">DJ Green Lantern</a>'s "Invasion Radio" in October 2011, French would call in to praise close friend and fellow-<a href="/wiki/Bronx" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronx">Bronx</a> rapper Fat Joe, revealing his role in helping to get "Shot Caller" on the airwaves.<sup id="cite_ref-FatJoeSiriusXM_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FatJoeSiriusXM-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Fat Joe, whom he refers to as "big brother", praised French's work ethic and revealed that French had been receiving offers from several major labels.<sup id="cite_ref-FatJoeSiriusXM_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FatJoeSiriusXM-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jim_Jones_bottle-throwing_incident">Jim Jones bottle-throwing incident</span></h4>
<p>On the night of August 5, 2011, <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">Bronx</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a> was slated to host <a href="/wiki/Funkmaster_Flex" title="Funkmaster Flex">Funkmaster Flex</a>'s birthday party at <a href="/wiki/Webster_Hall" title="Webster Hall">Webster Hall</a>. During his performance, Fat Joe brought out French Montana to perform on stage. Controversy erupted as Jim Jones and his entourage, who were reportedly on the adjacent balcony seats, began hurling bottles and glass at the performers.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The following day, videos of the incident were uploaded online, depicting French and his entourage facing a barrage of glass and liquor on stage, as they continued performing his rendition of "Hard In Da Paint" while facing the mentioned balcony with the crowd chanting along to it.<sup id="cite_ref-WebsterHall_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WebsterHall-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Some of the members on stage hurled debris back towards the balcony, as Jones and his entourage eventually exited the premises.<sup id="cite_ref-WebsterHall_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WebsterHall-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaborating_with_Diddy">Collaborating with Diddy</span></h4>
<p>Fat Joe and Waka Flocka accompanied French Montana in his video shoot for "Shot Caller" later that month in August. The song, which made reference to <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Diddy</a>'s 1997 hit "<a href="/wiki/Its_All_About_The_Benjamins" class="mw-redirect" title="Its All About The Benjamins">Its All About The Benjamins</a>", would soon garner the interest of the <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy</a> mogul. On October 9, French announced Diddy and <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a> for the official remix to the song.<sup id="cite_ref-ShotCallerRemix_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShotCallerRemix-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/DJ_Drama" title="DJ Drama">DJ Drama</a>, who called it his favorite record, referred T.I. to jump on the remix.<sup id="cite_ref-ShotCallerRemix_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShotCallerRemix-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Although the T.I. feature never came to fruition, the remix was released on November 24, and featured rappers Diddy and Rick Ross.
</p><p>With "Shot Caller" already one of the most played tracks on New York radio, on stations such as <a href="/wiki/Hot_97" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 97">Hot 97</a> and <a href="/wiki/Power_105" class="mw-redirect" title="Power 105">Power 105</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ShotCallerRemix_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShotCallerRemix-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> French was slated to appear on the upcoming episode of BET's <i><a href="/wiki/106_%26_Park" title="106 &amp; Park">106 &amp; Park</a></i> on December 6,<sup id="cite_ref-BadBoyKonvict_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BadBoyKonvict-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BETBadBoy_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BETBadBoy-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> where he would be debuting the music video and announcing the label he's signing with. Diddy would also appear that night as part of his "Bad Boy Takeover" campaign, whereon the two officially announced that French Montana had signed to Bad Boy Records.<sup id="cite_ref-BETBadBoy_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BETBadBoy-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Between 2011 and 2012, "Shot Caller" had become one of the most added tracks on <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban contemporary">urban contemporary</a> radio in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-SDinterview_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDinterview-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It was re-released as a single on January 10, and the music video for the remix was released in February 2012. A "NY Giants remix" premiered on <a href="/wiki/Funkmaster_Flex" title="Funkmaster Flex">Funkmaster Flex</a>'s radio show on January 6, celebrating the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">Giants</a>' <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl</a> win against the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">Patriots</a> the day before.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932016:_Signing_to_Bad_Boy_and_MMG"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012‚Äì2016:_Signing_to_Bad_Boy_and_MMG">2012‚Äì2016: Signing to Bad Boy and MMG</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Excuse_My_French_(album)" title="Excuse My French (album)">Excuse My French (album)</a></div>
<p>Having received offers from several labels, including Jay-Z's <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> and Kanye's <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a>; on December 6 on <a href="/wiki/BET" title="BET">BET</a>, French Montana publicly announced signing with Bad Boy Records, an imprint of <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>. In a subsequent interview with <a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a> magazine, French revealed that had he not signed with Bad Boy that MMG would be his next choice.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> However, on January 4, 2012, while in the studio with Rick Ross, the two announced French's new signing to a joint-venture between Bad Boy Records and Maybach Music Group, making him a part of both labels.<sup id="cite_ref-JointVenture_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JointVenture-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JointVenture2_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JointVenture2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Both Ross and Diddy would be executive producing his debut <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Studio album">studio album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JointVenture_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JointVenture-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JointVenture2_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JointVenture2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id=".22Stay_Schemin.22_and_.22Pop_That.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Stay_Schemin&quot;_and_&quot;Pop_That&quot;">"Stay Schemin" and "Pop That"</span></h4>
<p>On January 6, the two dropped Ross' track "<a href="/wiki/Stay_Schemin" class="mw-redirect" title="Stay Schemin">Stay Schemin</a>" with rapper <a href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a>. Notable for its memorable French and Ross "<a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a>", the track became one of the biggest hits that year, oft-talked about for its Drake verse believed to be a "diss" towards rapper <a href="/wiki/Common_(rapper)" title="Common (rapper)">Common</a> at the time. French Montana was featured on <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL's Freshman Class of 2012</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Ink" title="Kid Ink">Kid Ink</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Brown_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Danny Brown (rapper)">Danny Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macklemore" title="Macklemore">Macklemore</a>, Don Trip, <a href="/wiki/Hopsin" title="Hopsin">Hopsin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iggy_Azalea" title="Iggy Azalea">Iggy Azalea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roscoe_Dash" title="Roscoe Dash">Roscoe Dash</a>, and Bad Boy labelmate <a href="/wiki/Machine_Gun_Kelly_(musician)" title="Machine Gun Kelly (musician)">MGK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> French later revealed to host <a href="/wiki/Sway_Calloway" title="Sway Calloway">Sway Calloway</a> on MTV's <i>RapFix Live</i> in August 2012 that he almost turned down the cover opportunity feeling he deserved it a year or two prior.<sup id="cite_ref-RapFixLive_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RapFixLive-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>French's first single from the upcoming album, "<a href="/wiki/Pop_That" title="Pop That">Pop That</a>" was released on June 15, featuring Ross, Drake and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>. The song would be one of the biggest hits that year, and a still-popular club and summer anthem since. It is French's most successful commercial single, having been certified "<a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Music recording sales certification">platinum</a>" by the <a href="/wiki/RIAA" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA">RIAA</a>, and peaking at #2 on Billboard's <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hot_Rap_Songs" title="Hot Rap Songs">Rap</a> charts and #36 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a>. While initially expected for a release in July 2012, French's album went through several pushbacks until its finalized release date of May 21, 2013. The date which happened to coincide with the birthdays of Max B and famous labelmate the late <a href="/wiki/Notorious_B.I.G." class="mw-redirect" title="Notorious B.I.G.">Notorious B.I.G.</a> In the meantime, French had released his fifteenth mixtape <i>Coke Boys 3</i> on April 13, 2012, which included collaborations with fellow Coke Boys <a href="/wiki/Chinx_Drugz" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinx Drugz">Chinx Drugz</a> and Cheeze, alongside the likes of Ross, Akon, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Gates" title="Kevin Gates">Kevin Gates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>. Notable tracks among others include, a rare collaboration between French, Chinx and the late Stack Bundles on "Tap That", and "Headquarters" featuring <a href="/wiki/Red_Caf%C3%A9" title="Red Caf√©">Red Caf√©</a> and Chinx, the music video for which premiered on July 21.
</p>
<h4><span id="The_Homecoming_and_Mac_.26_Cheese_3"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Homecoming_and_Mac_&amp;_Cheese_3">The Homecoming and <i>Mac &amp; Cheese 3</i></span></h4>
<p>In September 2012, French Montana was featured on the cover of the 82nd issue of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fader" title="The Fader">The Fader</a></i> magazine,<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> who joined French on his first homecoming to Morocco after seventeen years since his family moved to the United States in 1996. The article describes his journey through Morocco, meeting his mother's family, and eventually his estranged father who is not made aware of his son's coming arrival.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> French was accompanied by manager Gaby Acevedo, and youngest brother Ayoub, in addition to Zach Baron and Michael Schmelling of <i>The Fader</i>. The piece ends with an emotional reunion between the father and the two sons, including Ayoub who had previously never met their father before.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>French marked the end of the year with his sixteenth mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Mac_%26_Cheese_3" title="Mac &amp; Cheese 3">Mac &amp; Cheese 3</a></i> released on November 20, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-FM16_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM16-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> which included collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Prodigy_(rapper)" title="Prodigy (rapper)">Prodigy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, Fat Joe, Ma$e, <a href="/wiki/Rico_Love" title="Rico Love">Rico Love</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trina" title="Trina">Trina</a> among others. Acclaimed for its production and track selection, it was among the most downloaded mixtapes of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-FM16_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM16-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> With several productions from <a href="/wiki/Young_Chop" title="Young Chop">Young Chop</a>, the music video to "Devil Wants My Soul" premiered on November 5, and an in-studio video of "Ocho Cinco" on November 26. Both songs would go viral, prompting another music video for "Ocho Cinco" ‚Äì featuring Diddy, <a href="/wiki/Machine_Gun_Kelly_(musician)" title="Machine Gun Kelly (musician)">MGK</a>, Red Caf√© and <a href="/wiki/King_Los" class="mw-redirect" title="King Los">King Los</a> ‚Äì released in February 2013. The song was also included as a bonus track on the upcoming <i><a href="/wiki/Excuse_My_French_(album)" title="Excuse My French (album)">Excuse My French</a></i> album. The run up to which included further video releases, including the Black Metaphor produced "Sanctuary" on February 3, <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a> produced "Diamonds" featuring Ross and <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a> on February 17, and Fraud produced "State of Mind" on May 15 and "Intro (Only If For A Night)" on November 30, among others. Since the tapes' premiere on <a href="/wiki/DatPiff" title="DatPiff">DatPiff</a>, it would reach the 500K "double platinum" rating by first month, and presently stands at a "diamond" rating with over 1.4 million downloads on that site alone.<sup id="cite_ref-FM16_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM16-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Excuse_My_French"><i>Excuse My French</i></span></h4>
<p>In January 2013, French announced his second single "<a href="/wiki/Freaks_(French_Montana_song)" title="Freaks (French Montana song)">Freaks</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, from his upcoming album to be a remake of <a href="/wiki/Vicious_(rapper)" title="Vicious (rapper)">Lil Vicious</a>' 1994 song of the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The song premiered on Hot 97 on February 13, with the music video coming out on March 3. The remix, featuring an additional Ross, Wale, <a href="/wiki/Mavado_(singer)" title="Mavado (singer)">Mavado</a> and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khaled" title="DJ Khaled">DJ Khaled</a>, was released on April 25. A bonus track "Marble Floors" was released earlier on December 4, 2012, featuring Ross, Lil Wayne and <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a> with production from <a href="/wiki/Mike_WiLL_Made_It" class="mw-redirect" title="Mike WiLL Made It">Mike WiLL Made It</a>. It would fast become a viral hit, only to be outdone by French's third single "<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_Worried_About_Nothin" class="mw-redirect" title="Ain&#39;t Worried About Nothin">Ain't Worried About Nothin</a>" released on April 15, 2013. The music video premiered on May 7, and would be the last before the release of his album on May 21. Subsequent music videos included, "Trap House" featuring Ross and <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(rapper)" title="Birdman (rapper)">Birdman</a> released on September 23, "Gifted" featuring <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">The Weeknd</a> on October 15, "Once In A While" featuring <a href="/wiki/Max_B" title="Max B">Max B</a> on November 18, and "Paranoid" featuring Johnny May Cash on January 20, 2014, among others.
</p><p>His first solo single "<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_Worried_About_Nothin" class="mw-redirect" title="Ain&#39;t Worried About Nothin">Ain't Worried About Nothin</a>" was a hit on radio stations, and a remix featuring Ross, Diddy and <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> was released on October 4, and a second remix featuring <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a> on October 14. Upon its release, <i>Excuse My French</i> was met with mixed reviews from music critics.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> It fared better commercially, debuting at number 4 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, with first-week sales of 56,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The album also featured collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Raekwon" title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarface_(rapper)" title="Scarface (rapper)">Scarface</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeremih" title="Jeremih">Jeremih</a> among others.
</p><p>Following the album release, French announced signing <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Durk" title="Lil Durk">Lil Durk</a> to his Coke Boys. French, who is close to producer <a href="/wiki/Young_Chop" title="Young Chop">Young Chop</a>, had previously collaborated with Durk on his recent mixtape and with Chief Keef on his debut album the year before. Durk, Chinx and Young Chop appeared in the music video to "Paranoid", featuring Chop's brother Johnny May Cash. The song is inspired by French's brushes with death, including the late-2003 incident where he survived a gunshot to the head. Durk collaborated on several records with French in the coming years, starting with the remix to Durk's breakout single "<a href="/wiki/Dis_Ain%27t_What_U_Want" class="mw-redirect" title="Dis Ain&#39;t What U Want">Dis Ain't What U Want</a>" featuring French, Ross and Meek Mill, released on November 27, 2013.
</p><p>French appeared as a featured artist on several singles in 2013, most notably <a href="/wiki/Joe_Budden" title="Joe Budden">Joe Budden</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/NBA_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA (song)">NBA</a>" with Wiz Khalifa released on March 26; <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Ferg" title="ASAP Ferg">ASAP Ferg</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Trap_Lord" title="Trap Lord">Work (Remix)</a>" ‚Äì alongside <a href="/wiki/Schoolboy_Q" title="Schoolboy Q">Schoolboy Q</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Rocky" title="ASAP Rocky">ASAP Rocky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_James" title="Trinidad James">Trinidad James</a> ‚Äì on May 14; Canadian singer <a href="/wiki/Massari" title="Massari">Massari</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Shisha_(song)" title="Shisha (song)">Shisha</a>" on May 21; and <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">Will.i.am</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Feelin%27_Myself_(will.i.am_song)" title="Feelin&#39; Myself (will.i.am song)">Feelin Myself</a>" with Miley Cyrus and Wiz Khalifa on November 26, among others.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pushbacks_and_comebacks">Pushbacks and comebacks</span></h4>
<p>Despite several pushbacks, French released his seventeenth mixtape <i>Coke Boys 4</i> on January 2, 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> which included collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machine_Gun_Kelly_(musician)" title="Machine Gun Kelly (musician)">MGK</a>, Mally Mall, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Durk" title="Lil Durk">Lil Durk</a> and MeetSims, among others. The music video for the "Paranoid (Remix)" ‚Äì featuring Diddy, Ross, Meek, Durk, Chinx and Jadakiss ‚Äì was released on April 13. Subsequent music videos included, "88 Coupes" featuring Jadakiss released on May 15, "God Body" featuring Chinx on May 28, and "Money Bag" with Durk and Chinx on June 23. In a January 2014 <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> interview, French revealed that his next <i>Mac &amp; Cheese</i> would be a studio album instead of a mixtape.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, French collaborated with Diddy on Ross' track "<a href="/wiki/Nobody_(Rick_Ross_song)" title="Nobody (Rick Ross song)">Nobody</a>" released on February 19. Rick Ross' remake of the late Notorious B.I.G.'s 1997 song "<a href="/wiki/Life_After_Death" title="Life After Death">You're Nobody (Til Somebody Kills You)</a>", featured an eerie chorus by French and interludes of Diddy in a live motivational rant. The song was inspired by Ross' brush against death the year before, when his <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Motors" title="Rolls-Royce Motors">Rolls-Royce</a> came under repeated gunshot fire while driving through <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, on January 28, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In a bizarre series of events, French Montana would experience a similar but unrelated event months later when his convoy came under fire on March 1 in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> during his "Excuse My French" tour after French had finished performing a show hours earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-MTVphilly2_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVphilly2-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CBSphilly_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSphilly-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The music video premiered on February 27, 2014. Albeit met with mixed to positive reviews, the song would be a hit and was re-released as a single on March 3, 2014. French joined Ross for a live performance on the television program <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Night_with_Seth_Meyers" title="Late Night with Seth Meyers">Late Night with Seth Meyers</a></i> on March 5, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>French Montana would collaborate with fellow-Bronx native <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a> on her comeback single "<a href="/wiki/I_Luh_Ya_Papi" title="I Luh Ya Papi">I Luh Ya Papi</a>". The song premiered on LA's <a href="/wiki/Power_106" class="mw-redirect" title="Power 106">Power 106</a> on March 5, and was released as a single on March 11, with the music video coming out two days later. The single was an international hit, and among the most added/played tracks on <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_contemporary" title="Rhythmic contemporary">rhythmic contemporary</a> radio in Canada. French also appeared in the music video to Fat Joe's single "Stressin", featuring Jennifer Lopez, which premiered in October later that year. French joined Rick Ross on <a href="/wiki/Puff_Daddy" class="mw-redirect" title="Puff Daddy">Puff Daddy</a>'s comeback single "Big Homie" from his upcoming album <i>MMM</i>. With a guest verse by Ross and ad-libs by French, the single was released on March 24, with the music video premiering on March 31. French Montana joined Ross, Meek and veteran <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> on <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khaled" title="DJ Khaled">DJ Khaled</a>'s summer hit "<a href="/wiki/They_Don%27t_Love_You_No_More" title="They Don&#39;t Love You No More">They Don't Love You No More</a>". The single was released on March 29, with the music video coming out on June 22 that year.
</p><p>On July 17, teasers to the movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Purge:_Anarchy" title="The Purge: Anarchy">The Purge: Anarchy</a></i> were released featuring music from French's upcoming single "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Panic_(French_Montana_song)" title="Don&#39;t Panic (French Montana song)">Don't Panic</a>". A month earlier, Instagram photos of the two showed French with then-girlfriend <a href="/wiki/Khlo%C3%A9_Kardashian" title="Khlo√© Kardashian">Khlo√© Kardashian</a> on set with matching masks on, prompting speculation whether she was in the coming video. Following weeks of promotion, the single was released on August 12. The music video, which retained the dark themes of the movie while maintaining its catchy <a href="/wiki/DJ_Mustard" class="mw-redirect" title="DJ Mustard">DJ Mustard</a> character, became a viral hit. The couple had created bit of a stir two months earlier, on June 2, when Khlo√© posted an IG photo of the two on set of "They Don't Love You No More", depicting French holding a rifle in his arms with Khlo√© seated next to him with a bottle of liquor to her mouth. The remix to "Don't Panic", featuring Jeremih and Chris Brown, was released on October 14.
</p><p>French Montana would join <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a> on DJ Khaled's "They Don't Love You No More (Remix)" released on August 2. Khaled's former <a href="/wiki/Terror_Squad_(group)" title="Terror Squad (group)">Terror Squad</a> affiliate and Bronx-native Remy Ma had just been released from prison the day prior. The three appeared together in the music video which premiered on August 23.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> This was her first musical comeback since her incarceration six years earlier. French collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a> on her second single "<a href="/wiki/Braveheart_(Ashanti_album)" title="Braveheart (Ashanti album)">Early In The Morning</a>" released on October 14 off of her comeback album, <i>Braveheart</i>. This would be Ashanti's first album in six years.
</p><p>French released his second single "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Bitch" title="Bad Bitch">Bad Bitch</a>", featuring Jeremih, in December 2014, with the music video premiering on February 23, 2015. In late-October, French had announced his "Set It Off" tour with Jeremih, running up to his expected <i>Mac &amp; Cheese: The Album</i> release in December. With the album eventually pushed back to next year; in its place, French released his collaborative <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> with Harry Fraud, <i>Mac &amp; Cheese: The Appetizer</i> on December 12, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FM18_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM18-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> His eighteenth mixtape, <i>The Appetizer</i> marked a shift away from French's usual feature-heavy records. With Fraud's signature sample-heavy production, French blurred the lines between rap and R&amp;B in a manner not unlike that of Max B, and with subject matter ranging from difficult life-decisions, women, addiction and memories of his bygone friendship with his now-incarcerated rap soulmate. In August 2015, French paired with pop-opera artist <a href="/wiki/Charisse_Mills" title="Charisse Mills">Charisse Mills</a> for the single "Champagne."<sup id="cite_ref-allhiphop_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allhiphop-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2016.E2.80.93present:_Wave_Gods.2C_MC4.2C_Jungle_Rules.2C_Montana.2C_They_Got_Amnesia"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016‚Äìpresent:_Wave_Gods,_MC4,_Jungle_Rules,_Montana,_They_Got_Amnesia">2016‚Äìpresent: <i>Wave Gods</i>, <i>MC4</i>, <i>Jungle Rules</i>, <i>Montana, They Got Amnesia</i></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Jungle_Rules" title="Jungle Rules">Jungle Rules</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montana_(album)" title="Montana (album)">Montana (album)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/They_Got_Amnesia" title="They Got Amnesia">They Got Amnesia</a></div>
<p>On February 14, 2016, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khaled" title="DJ Khaled">DJ Khaled</a> announced that he would debut French's new mixtape on <a href="/wiki/We_The_Best" class="mw-redirect" title="We The Best">We The Best</a> Radio.<sup id="cite_ref-DJ_Khaled_to_premiere_French_Montana&#39;s_mixtape_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DJ_Khaled_to_premiere_French_Montana&#39;s_mixtape-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape, hosted by Max B, debuted on February 19, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On May 5, 2016, French's contract with Interscope and MMG ended, and he later signed a joint venture record deal with Bad Boy and <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Later, French was going to release his second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/MC4_(mixtape)" title="MC4 (mixtape)">MC4</a></i> in October 2016, however, the album's release was canceled after <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a> unofficially released the album on <a href="/wiki/Compact_disc" title="Compact disc">CD</a> on its original release date (August 19, 2016), two months before the album was set to release, which also managed to leak its entirety on internet as a <a href="/wiki/Music_leak" title="Music leak">leak</a>, plus some "sample clearance issues" on tracks like "I'm Heated" and 2 Times".<sup id="cite_ref-Scrapped_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scrapped-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> It was originally supposed to be the fourth installment in the "Mac &amp; Cheese" series, and the first to be originally released as an album. French later stated that he's planning to start a new record label with Max B when he is released. On November 5, 2016, Montana unexpectedly released the album as a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> instead and premiered it on <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Beats_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Beats 1">Beats 1</a> radio show, <a href="/wiki/OVO_Sound" title="OVO Sound">OVO Sound</a> radio later that night. Montana revealed in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Zane_Lowe" title="Zane Lowe">Zane Lowe</a> on his <a href="/wiki/Beats_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Beats 1">Beats 1</a> radio show that the first and second single from his upcoming project is ready to be released. He also announced a collaborative track with <a href="/wiki/Chance_the_Rapper" title="Chance the Rapper">Chance the Rapper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quavo" title="Quavo">Quavo</a>, produced by Ben Billions, a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Swae_Lee" title="Swae Lee">Swae Lee</a> that is "just like 'Unforgettable'", as well as a song called "No Stylist".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> On July 14, 2017, Montana released <i><a href="/wiki/Jungle_Rules" title="Jungle Rules">Jungle Rules</a></i> as his second album.
</p><p>On December 6, 2019, French Montana released his third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Montana_(album)" title="Montana (album)">Montana</a></i>, which includes the song "<a href="/wiki/Writing_on_the_Wall_(French_Montana_song)" title="Writing on the Wall (French Montana song)">Writing on the Wall</a>", a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Cardi_B" title="Cardi B">Cardi B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post_Malone" title="Post Malone">Post Malone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rvssian" title="Rvssian">Rvssian</a>.
</p><p>Montana's fourth studio album, <a href="/wiki/They_Got_Amnesia" title="They Got Amnesia">They Got Amnesia</a> was released through Epic Records on November 19, 2021, including the singles "FMWGAB", "I Don't Really Care", "Panicking", a collaboration with American rapper <a href="/wiki/Fivio_Foreign" title="Fivio Foreign">Fivio Foreign</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/Handstand_(song)" title="Handstand (song)">Handstand</a>", a collaboration with American rapper and singers <a href="/wiki/Doja_Cat" title="Doja Cat">Doja Cat</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Saweetie" title="Saweetie">Saweetie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>French Montana, on June 9, 2022, released a song "Je M'appelle" with fellow Moroccan-British artist Benzz and <a href="/wiki/Tion_Wayne" title="Tion Wayne">Tion Wayne</a>.
</p><p>In 2023, the documentary "For Khadija" premiered at the <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Festival" title="Tribeca Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Directed by Mandon Lovett and co-executive produced by <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean "Diddy" Combes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> the film documents the story of his family's emigration from Morocco to New York,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and explores the plight of his single immigrant mother raising three sons and his rise to success as a recording artist.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span></h2>
<p>French Montana's career has been the subject of many allegations of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_misconduct" title="Sexual misconduct">sexual misconduct</a> in the 2020s, the earliest of which date back years. Several women accused him of <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drug-facilitated_sexual_assault" title="Drug-facilitated sexual assault">drug-facilitated sexual assault</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_battery" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual battery">sexual battery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_misconduct" title="Sexual misconduct">sexual misconduct</a>, allegations he denies, for which the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_limitations" title="Statute of limitations">statute of limitations</a> either did not apply or had not elapsed, in nearly all cases. In March 2020, French Montana was accused of raping an <a href="/wiki/Unconsciousness" title="Unconsciousness">incapacitated</a> woman at his former home in <a href="/wiki/Hidden_Hills,_California" title="Hidden Hills, California">Hidden Hills, California</a>. Montana was sued by a woman using the pseudonym <i>"<a href="/wiki/Jane_Doe" class="mw-redirect" title="Jane Doe">Jane Doe</a>"</i>, for <a href="/wiki/Assault" title="Assault">assault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battery_(crime)" title="Battery (crime)">battery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_battery" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual battery">sexual battery</a>, intentional infliction of <a href="/wiki/Emotional_distress" class="mw-redirect" title="Emotional distress">emotional distress</a>, negligent hiring, supervision and retention and <a href="/wiki/Negligence" title="Negligence">negligence</a>, in connection to a March 28, 2018, incident reported to police in which the woman alleged Montana drugged her and raped her while she was incapacitated on his bathroom floor. The suit alleged Montana "would sometimes without the women's knowledge or consent provide drugs to interfere with the women's ability to knowingly consent to sexual activity and had a longstanding practice of inviting women to his recording sessions, or choosing women at bars." Montana allegedly supplied women with drinks and drugs, "with the purpose of engaging in sexual acts with them, without any regard to whether or not they consented, or were able to consent." According to her court filing, "Kharbouch (French Montana) was one of the men who entered the room and sexually assaulted her". Doe reported the alleged rape to the police that same day and had a rape kit administered;  a subsequent police investigation showed the presence of semen.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Independent_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Independent-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Variety_1_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety_1-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-XXL_50_Cent_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXL_50_Cent-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Us_Magazine_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Us_Magazine-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oxygen_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxygen-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2021, Montana was accused of sexual assault by a second woman, Sarah Kamilla, a <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan people">Moroccan</a> model, who said Montana cornered her and attempted to rape her while she was in the bathroom during a dinner party hosted by <a href="/wiki/Palestinian" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian">Palestinian</a> rapper <a href="/wiki/Belly_(rapper)" title="Belly (rapper)">Belly</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/W_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="W Hotel">W Hotel</a> in Miami in 2017 when she was a teenager at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-Perez_Hilton_1_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perez_Hilton_1-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Morocco_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Morocco-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Observateur_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observateur-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Montana was then accused of sexual assault by a third woman, Kayla Rose, in 2021 who alleged that he sexually assaulted her while she was in the bathroom in a hotel room in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a> in 2018. Rose later filed a police report following the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-Kayla_Rose_Rape_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kayla_Rose_Rape-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Observateur_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observateur-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Perez_Hilton_1_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perez_Hilton_1-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Morocco_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Morocco-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Us_Magazine_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Us_Magazine-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Variety_1_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety_1-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Independent_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Independent-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, French Montana committed plagiarism. Montana copied and pasted the first verse of <a href="/wiki/Astrid_S" title="Astrid S">Astrid S</a>' song "Jump" into the track "How You King?", without permission.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Astrid S retroactively got proper attribution as a co-songwriter and received compensation for the lyrics that were plagiarized.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h2>
<p>Montana's charitable work started after he visited Uganda to film his "<a href="/wiki/Unforgettable_(French_Montana_song)" title="Unforgettable (French Montana song)">Unforgettable</a>" video in 2017, a song that gained over a billion streams and held strong on the top 10 in the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. His efforts in Uganda raised roughly US$500,000 to build the Suubi hospital which serves over 300,000 citizens of Uganda.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, French was named an Ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Global_Citizen_(organization)" title="Global Citizen (organization)">Global Citizen</a> following his charitable donation of $100,000 for a hospital in <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In 2022, it was reported that he helped raise over US$220 million for Uganda's maternal healthcare services. He received a 2022 Innovator Award for his efforts the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Montana is fluent in his <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Morocco" title="Languages of Morocco">native</a> Arabic and French as well as in English.<sup id="cite_ref-fader_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StatusMag_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatusMag-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> He cites being a father as one of his driving inspirations.<sup id="cite_ref-StatusMag_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatusMag-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> He is a practicing <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montana has been a resident of the <a href="/wiki/Pompton_Plains,_New_Jersey" title="Pompton Plains, New Jersey">Pompton Plains</a> section of <a href="/wiki/Pequannock_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Pequannock Township, New Jersey">Pequannock Township, New Jersey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, he bought <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Calabasas,_California" title="Calabasas, California">Calabasas</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> home for $3.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montana married Deen Kharbouch in 2007. The couple had separated by 2012, and their divorce was finalized in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worried_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worried-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> They have a son who was born in October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-worried_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worried-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, Montana became a <a href="/wiki/Citizen_of_the_United_States_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizen of the United States of America">U.S. citizen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting_incident">Shooting incident</span></h3>
<p>In 2003, two gunmen shot at Montana as he left a recording studio in New York, striking him in the head.<sup id="cite_ref-Life+Times_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life+Times-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CombatJack3_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CombatJack3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He survived and was hospitalized for several weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-USmag_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USmag-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> One of the gunmen died during the incident, in what is believed to be a case of "<a href="/wiki/Friendly_fire" title="Friendly fire">friendly fire</a>" by one assailant against the other. Montana was investigated for the incident, but the case was eventually dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CombatJack3_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CombatJack3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In early 2013, Montana visited the site of the shooting with a camera crew from Life+Times as he recalled the near-death experience and his life growing up in the Bronx. This was the first time he had visited the location since the attempted murder ten years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-Life+Times_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life+Times-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> According to French, he was set up by someone close to him and his circle.<sup id="cite_ref-Life+Times_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life+Times-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exotic_pets">Exotic pets</span></h3>
<p>French has been the owner of a number of pets, ranging from dogs to exotic animals such as <a href="/wiki/Tigers" class="mw-redirect" title="Tigers">tigers</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">monkey</a>. On April 22, 2013, French Montana posted an Instagram picture with the caption "Got so high last night bought 2 baby tigers". The picture was of French outdoors holding two tiger cubs, one on each arm.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The tigers, named Ike and Tina, were prominently featured in French's music video for "<a href="/wiki/Excuse_My_French_(album)" title="Excuse My French (album)">The Gifted</a>" featuring friend and singer <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">The Weeknd</a>, released later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>  In 2014, the rapper noted he had given up the two tigers shortly after getting them, citing the difficulty in feeding and caring for the animals.<sup id="cite_ref-Ridiculousness_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ridiculousness-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since late-2014, French Montana became the owner of a pet monkey named Julius Ceasor. A video of the animal was uploaded on December 18, showing French and record producer Mally Mall entering a private-jet with French then cradling the infant monkey in his arms.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_influences">Musical influences</span></h2>
<p>French Montana describes <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a> among the hip hop artists he listened to growing up.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexWIFM_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexWIFM-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StatusMag_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatusMag-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BallerStatus2012_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BallerStatus2012-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> He considers himself a music lover in general, and admires the work of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> soul/R&amp;B singers <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse" title="Amy Winehouse">Amy Winehouse</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-StatusMag_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatusMag-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> the English rock band <a href="/wiki/Florence_%2B_the_Machine" class="mw-redirect" title="Florence + the Machine">Florence + the Machine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hot97single2_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hot97single2-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> and American singer <a href="/wiki/Lana_Del_Rey" title="Lana Del Rey">Lana Del Rey</a>, several of whom he has sampled in his music.
</p>
